headers.remove(header);\n152:   }\n153: \n154:   // Temporary storage to hold evaluated values of headers to add and replace. This is required\n155:   // to execute all formatters using the original received headers.\n156:   // Only after all the formatters produced the new values of the headers, the headers are set.\n157:   // absl::InlinedVector is optimized for 4 headers. After that it behaves as normal std::vector.\n158:   // It is assumed that most of the use cases will add or modify fairly small number of headers\n159:   // (<=4). If this assumption changes, the number of inlined capacity should be increased.\n160:   // header_formatter_speed_test.cc provides micro-benchmark for evaluating speed of adding and\n161:   // replacing headers and should be used when modifying the code below to access the performance\n162:   // impact of code changes.\n163:   absl::InlinedVector<std::pair<const Http::LowerCaseString&, const std::string>, 4> headers_to_add,\n164:       headers_to_overwrite;\n165:   // value_buffer is used only when stream_info is a valid pointer and stores header value\n166:   // created by a formatter. It is declared outside of 'for' loop for performance reason to avoid\n167:   // stack allocation and unnecessary std::string's memory adjustments for each iteration. The\n168:   // actual value of the header is accessed via 'value' variable which is initialized differently\n169:   // depending whether stream_info and valid or nullptr. Based on performance tests implemented in\n170:   // header_formatter_speed_test.cc this approach strikes the best balance between performance and\n171:   // readability.\n172:   std::string value_buffer;\n173:   for (const auto& [key, entry] : headers_to_add_) {\n174:     absl::string_view value;\n175:     if (stream_info != nullptr) {\n176:       value_buffer = entry->formatter_->formatWithContext(context, *stream_info);\n177:       value = value_buffer;\n178:     } else {\n179:       value = entry->original_value_;\n180:     }\n181:     if (!value.empty() || entry->add_if_empty_) {\n182:       switch (entry->append_action_) {\n183:         PANIC_ON_PROTO_ENUM_SENTINEL_VALUES;\n184:       case HeaderValueOption::APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD:\n185:         headers_to_add.emplace_back(key, value);\n186:         break;\n187:       case HeaderValueOption::ADD_IF_ABSENT:\n188:         if (auto header_entry = headers.get(key); But what about local replies?\n\nWhen a local reply is sent by the router (e.g., no cluster found), the flow is:\n1. Router calls `callbacks_->sendLocalReply(code, body, modify_headers_, ...)`\n2. Filter manager's sendLocalReply is called\n3. In filter manager, it wraps the modify_headers callback and calls Utility::sendLocalReply\n\nThe wrapped callback in filter_manager.cc (lines 1072-1078, 1123-1129, 1156-1162) is:\n```cpp\n[this, modify_headers](ResponseHeaderMap& headers) -> void {\n  if (streamInfo().route() && streamInfo().route()->routeEntry()) {\n    streamInfo().route()->routeEntry()->finalizeResponseHeaders(headers, streamInfo());\n  }\n  if (modify_headers) {\n    modify_headers(headers);\n  }\n}\n```\n\nSo this wrapping lambda calls:\n1. `finalizeResponseHeaders` - which applies route-level response headers\n2. `modify_headers` - which is the router's modify_headers_ lambda\n\nAnd this is passed as the `modify_headers` callback to `Utility::sendLocalReply`.\n\nInside `Utility::prepareLocalReply` (line 718-720):\n```cpp\nif (encode_functions.modify_headers_) {\n  encode_functions.modify_headers_(*response_headers);\n}\n```\n\nThis invokes the wrapped lambda, which applies `finalizeResponseHeaders` and then the router's `modify_headers_`. So route-level response headers get added once at this point. The header_mutation filter applies its own configured headers separately, not the route-level ones.\n\nLet me reconsider the duplication issue.
